The pattern matches the post-mortem topography of working-class neighborhoods that have lost a public figure to violence (compare the murals for Biggie in Brooklyn, for community shooting victims across the country): the **physical infrastructure becomes the memory infrastructure**.

The grief is then, in the resurrection arc (*Fallen Friend*, the X-Men *Hellfire Gala* sequence, and Kamala's mutant rebirth on Krakoa/Arakko-adjacent terms), partially **complicated rather than relieved**. The neighborhood was not consulted on the resurrection. The kid came back, but came back through a process Manhattan and Krakoa controlled. Greenville's emotional posture toward the resurrection, as observable in subsequent panels, is **wary gratitude with an undertone of dispossession** — *we mourned her properly; you brought her back without us*. This is the seed of a low-grade civic resentment that persists to the present.

---

## iv. The post-resurrection settlement (2023–24)

The neighborhood reabsorbs Kamala but the terms of reabsorption are quietly altered. Several observable changes in the published record:

- **Reduced civilian wave-frequency.** In the pre-death panels, residents wave to Ms. Marvel from stoops with a kind of casual proprietary warmth. Post-resurrection panels show a *slight but consistent attenuation* — fewer waves, more nods, more eyes-following-without-engaging. The subject is processing the strangeness of having mourned someone who walks past again.
- **Shift in the mural ecology.** The original death-period murals are not painted over but are *not refreshed* with the same urgency. New murals appear that frame Kamala as **mutant-among-many** rather than as Greenville's singular daughter. This represents a partial cession of the symbol to a wider mutant iconography — and a partial loss for the neighborhood, which had owned her exclusively.
- **The Circle Q's role consolidates.** Bruno's old store, under post-Bruno-departure management arrangements (Bruno's life trajectory through Wakanda and back is family-adjacent rather than residential by this point), now operates as the *de facto* civic-memory anchor. It is the building the neighborhood would defend first if forced to choose.

---

## v. The development pressure: Hope Yards 2.0 and successor vehicles (ongoing)

The Worthy-era developers were defeated as personalities but never as capital. The current era of the record shows the development threat **mutating into less personalized, more bureaucratized forms**: shell LLCs acquiring tax-lien properties along the waterfront and the rail corridor; "opportunity zone" branding (real-world legal regime referenced obliquely in Greenville-set panels); and the slow disappearance of small businesses replaced by units whose signage is in a different typographic register — the visual grammar of gentrification rendered as background world-building.

The neighborhood's defenses are tuned, per Section 5, to **dramatic threats, not actuarial ones**, and the current development pressure is precisely the actuarial kind. There is no Chuck Worthy to punch. The threat is a property-tax assessment, a zoning variance, a quietly approved permit. The published record shows the subject **under-responding** to this threat relative to its acute-threat response capacity — town halls are held, op-eds are written by aunties and by the Coles civics teacher, but there is no equivalent of the Inventor-era mass mobilization, because the threat does not look like a threat in the neighborhood's threat-recognition grammar.

This is the most clinically concerning current condition. The subject is being **slowly hollowed by a stressor it is constitutionally bad at recognizing**.

Specific markers of the hollowing, observable in recent background art:

- A noticeable increase in **scaffolding panels** in establishing shots — Greenville is being renovated *upward*, not maintained *outward*.
- The appearance of **chain coffee storefronts** at intersections previously held by independent businesses.
- A subtle shift in the **crowd composition** of background panels: more young-professional silhouettes, fewer halal-cart-and-stroller compositions in the corridors closest to the PATH.
- The **disappearance of certain recurring extras** — the elderly Polish gentleman who walked the same block in Wilson-era panels has not been seen in current-era issues, and while this could be a continuity drift, it functions in-universe as the depopulation pattern any longitudinal observer of gentrification would clock.

---

## vi. The Khan family's current configuration

The neighborhood's emotional weather is partially set by the Khan household, which functions as a **barometric site** the rest of Greenville reads. Current state:

- **Yusuf Khan** has aged into the neighborhood's senior-uncle stratum. His public presence has narrowed to mosque-and-home routes; his health is not foregrounded but his pace in background panels is slower.
- **Muneeba Khan** has expanded her civic footprint — more visible at mosque committee functions, more central in the aunty-network whose informal authority over the block is total.
- **Aamir and Tyesha**'s household provides Greenville its current-era *next-generation child*, whose presence in panels signals neighborhood continuity. The wedding the neighborhood threw is now the family it watches grow up; this is the kind of multi-decade continuity Greenville treats as load-bearing.
- **Kamala herself** is now a more itinerant resident — Krakoan/X-adjacent obligations, Champions residue, the periodic Avengers-adjacent guest appearance. She returns. She does not always sleep in her old bedroom. The neighborhood notices.
- **Bruno** is operationally elsewhere (Wakanda-residue, intermittent returns). The Circle Q's day-to-day is handled by family arrangements and by ambient community presence. His absence is one of the quiet wounds of the current era — the neighborhood lost its second-favorite kid to circumstance, not death, and the muted grief of that loss is harder to memorialize.
- **Nakia, Zoe, Mike, Gabe** — the friend-cohort has dispersed into late-twenties trajectories, returning home in the rhythms of working-class adult children: holidays, crises, weddings.

---

## vii. The mosque and faith infrastructure: current state

The Islamic Center remains the single most stable institution in the neighborhood's published architecture. Sheikh Abdullah is older but still depicted as functional; the mosque's program — youth, food assistance, post-prayer counseling — operates at the same competence level as in the Wilson era. If anything, the mosque has *gained* function as municipal services have receded under development pressure; it is increasingly the de facto social-services anchor for residents who do not trust the formal apparatus.

Observable current-era mosque behaviors:
- **Coordination with Catholic and AME congregations** in the neighborhood for joint food-distribution programs (background mentions, ambient signage).
- **Continued absorption of post-9/11-residual federal interest** — the surveillance posture of relevant agencies toward American Muslim institutions is canonically referenced and remains a low-grade chronic stressor.
- **Intergenerational programming** that has begun to include the second generation of Wilson-era kids: today's mosque youth are the younger siblings of Kamala's cohort, growing up under the *long shadow of her example*. The neighborhood is producing a generation that has known Ms. Marvel as ambient civic fact since infancy.

---

## viii. Coles Academic High and the school system

Coles continues to function as depicted, with the HVAC still failing on schedule, the lockers still graffitied in the specific Coles-graffiti vocabulary, and the same staff archetypes recognizable across runs. The school's current pressure points:

- **Test-score regimes** and the chronic threat of state-level reorganization (Greenville-set panels include passing references to standardized-testing anxiety that map to real-world New Jersey education politics).
- **The post-Kamala alumni mythology** — Coles now carries the weight of having graduated Ms. Marvel, and this is treated by current students with the mixture of pride and eye-rolling that any school carries about its famous alumna.
- **Recruitment interest from "talent identification" programs** of dubious origin — current arcs hint at Orchis-adjacent or corporate-funded outreach to identify mutant or super-powered students. The school's administrative posture toward this is depicted as guarded, which is itself a Greenville-style response (institutional caution from a building whose HVAC doesn't work but whose principal is not stupid).

---

## ix. The light-rail corridor and the waterfront

The HBLR corridor remains the neighborhood's circulatory spine. Recent panels show:
- Increased ridership of **non-resident character** — Manhattan-bound professionals reverse-commuting through Greenville as cheaper origin.
- The waterfront, previously brownfield-coded, partially **redeveloped** in the post-Inventor period. The relic-and-warehouse aesthetic of the Wilson-era waterfront has been overwritten in some panels with glass-and-concrete residential. This is not universally celebrated within the neighborhood.

The **Hudson-facing skyline of Manhattan** remains the neighborhood's permanent visual interlocutor. Greenville lives across the river from the franchise's center of gravity and is shown, in establishing shots, *with Manhattan in the background* with such consistency that the river itself functions as a character — the moat the neighborhood lives behind, both a barrier and a reminder.

---

## x. The current threat ecology

Synthesizing the published evidence of the last ~24 months of in-universe time, the neighborhood faces a **stratified threat profile**:

1. **Acute superhuman:** Lower than peak Wilson-era. Greenville is no longer the surprise destination for second-tier antagonists hunting Ms. Marvel; she is now mobile enough that her enemies follow her elsewhere. *This is partial protection by absence.*
2. **Mutant-political:** Elevated. Orchis-residue, corporate scanning, ambient hate-crime weather. The neighborhood is now exposed to a hostility class it did not previously carry.
3. **Federal-surveillance (post-9/11 residue):** Chronic, low-grade, persistent. The Aamir-detention precedent has not been forgotten.
4. **Capital/development:** **Highest current threat by long-term displacement potential.** Insufficiently recognized by the neighborhood's own threat-grammar.
5. **Climate:** Quietly rising. Jersey City's coastal exposure to storm surge is not foregrounded in canon but is implicit in any longitudinal view of the waterfront. Hurricane-residue panels occasionally surface in background art.
6. **Internal:** Generational drift, the slow loss of the Wilson-era cohort to adult life elsewhere, the question of whether the next generation will stay or commute outward.

---

## xi. Current civic personality assessment

Comparing the current-state behavioral record to the baseline established in Sections 3–5, the subject presents the following modulations:

- **Defenses largely intact.** Humor, altruism, sublimation continue at expected baseline. The Vaillant-hierarchy profile from Section 3 holds.
- **Grief load elevated but contained.** The death-and-return of Ms. Marvel is processed and continues to be processed. The neighborhood has demonstrated that it can survive bereavement of a load-bearing local hero, which is itself a developmental milestone.
- **Mild new symptom: dispossession affect.** The slight cooling of civilian engagement with Kamala, the cession of her symbol to wider mutant iconography, the unconsulted resurrection — these together produce a low-grade *we are no longer the sole keepers* affect. This is mournful but not maladaptive.
- **Under-recognized vulnerability worsening.** The actuarial-displacement threat continues to grow without commensurate civic mobilization.
- **Faith and mutual-aid infrastructure load-bearing more than ever.** As municipal and federal services thin under development-era reorganization, the mosque, the bodega-network, and the aunty-network are carrying more weight per capita.
- **Generational succession in progress.** The Wilson-era teenagers are now adults; the next layer of Greenville children is being raised under their long shadow. The neighborhood is reproducing itself, which is the most important current vital sign.

---

## xii. Where they are now

The neighborhood, at the present moment of the published record, is **alive, alert, slightly tired, slightly thinner around the edges, and still recognizably itself**. It has buried and exhumed its most famous daughter, watched its kids leave and return, fought off a developer by name only to face his successors in unbranded form, accommodated a taxonomic reclassification of its embedded hero without losing its grip on her, and continued to operate its mosque, its bodega, its school, and its stoops at the same level of mutual-aid competence that has defined it since 2014.

It is **not in crisis**. It is in the slower and more dangerous condition of **chronic adjustment to a series of pressures that do not announce themselves dramatically**. The Inventor came with robots; the developer comes with a permit application. Greenville knows how to fight the first. The published record is currently watching, in real time, whether it will learn to fight the second.

The dossier's current-state finding: **the subject is functionally stable, structurally threatened, emotionally adult, and historically continuous with itself in a way that few Marvel locations achieve.** Whatever the next arc brings — and the editorial pattern suggests another acute event is statistically due — the neighborhood will, by all available behavioral evidence, **respond first by clustering at the Circle Q**, and proceed from there.

Watch the bodega. The bodega tells you everything.


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY

## SUBJECT: JERSEY CITY NEIGHBORHOOD (Greenville, Marvel-616) — Somatic & Infrastructural Casefile

---

## I. PREAMBLE: THE BODY OF THE NEIGHBORHOOD

The subject's "body" must be read across four overlapping anatomical systems, each with its own clinical history:

1. **Skeletal-structural** — the building stock: pre-war brownstones in the residential corridor, the mid-century commercial spine along the avenues, the Coles Academic High campus, the Islamic Center, the Circle Q at the corner of the Khan family's block, the waterfront industrial belt, and the elevated/light-rail infrastructure that tethers the body to Manhattan.
2. **Circulatory** — the PATH train, the Hudson-Bergen Light Rail, the bus lines, the Holland Tunnel feeders, and the daily commuter outflow/inflow.
3. **Soft tissue** — the residents themselves, the demographic mass, the pediatric population concentrated around Coles and the mosque's youth programs.
4. **Microbiome / interstitial** — the bodegas, halal carts, dry cleaners, hookah cafés, Pakistani bakeries, Polish butchers, Dominican salons, the small-business mesh that does the actual metabolic work.

What follows is the longitudinal medical record across these systems from approximately 2014 (the subject's first foregrounded appearance) through the 2023 bereavement event and into the recovery phase.

---

## II. CHRONIC CONDITIONS (LONGITUDINAL)

### A. Chronic Infrastructural Undernourishment

A clinical baseline. Across nearly every depicted panel of street-level Greenville, the built environment presents with the stigmata of long-term capital deprivation:

- **Sidewalk dermatology:** cracked slabs, tree-root upheaval, ad-hoc concrete patches in mismatched colors at the curbs near the Circle Q. The hex-tile sections nearer the older brownstones are spalled at corner intersections — a sign that no municipal tile replacement program has run in a decade-plus.
- **Façade pathology:** taped bodega windows (a recurring visual), rolling-gate rust at the base where street salt accumulates, faded mural ghosting on the brick sides of corner buildings, exterior conduit run *outside* the wall (a marker of cheaper retrofit electrical work — interior fishing was skipped).
- **HVAC chronicity at Coles Academic High:** the school's climate system is depicted as perennially failing — windows propped open in winter, students fanning themselves in late spring, the gym smelling of itself. This is not a one-issue gag; it recurs across writers and is the most reliable single biomarker of municipal under-investment.
- **Streetlight intermittence:** sodium-vapor fixtures dominate where LED conversion has occurred in Manhattan and the better-funded Hudson County corridors. Several panels show one-bulb-out, one-bulb-on patterning along residential streets.
- **Hydrant and curb-cut neglect:** ADA compliance is patchwork; older corners lack truncated domes.
- **Roofing:** the Khan brownstone and several adjacent buildings show patched flat-roof membranes visible in establishing shots — a multi-decade record of leak-and-tar interventions rather than full replacement.

*Clinical impact:* the subject lives in a body that **aches in low frequencies, constantly**. There is no acute pain crisis — it is the somatic equivalent of untreated osteoarthritis. The psychological consequence is a **normalization of discomfort**, which feeds the broader pattern of under-naming structural harm.

### B. Commuter-Extractive Circulatory Disorder

The PATH and light-rail dependency for Manhattan-bound labor creates what is, in human-medical terms, a **diurnal hypovolemic syndrome**: every weekday morning the neighborhood loses a significant fraction of its working-age vascular volume across the Hudson, returning depleted in the evening.

- Morning Journal Square and Exchange Place platforms show panel-confirmed peak crush; evening returns show fatigue postures.
- The local economy operates in **off-peak hours** — bodegas, restaurants, and youth programming run on a schedule shifted later than Manhattan's, accommodating the returning workforce.
- The light rail's Greenville-area stations are depicted as less-renovated than the Hoboken/Newport end of the line, mirroring infrastructural gradient.

*Clinical impact:* energy and adult presence are time-shifted. Adolescents are alone-with-the-neighborhood for substantial windows each day — which is why the youth-centered emergency response patterns evolved as they did. The neighborhood **raises its young in the gap between commutes.**

### C. Brownfield / Toxic Exposure History

The waterfront and industrial corridor is the subject's **liver** — both filter and accumulator of historical insult.

- **Pre-published baseline:** historic industrial use along the Hudson edge (manufacturing, rail yards, port operations) implies a century of soil and groundwater contamination that no panel addresses but every panel inherits.
- **The Inventor era:** lair sited in the abandoned industrial belt, with bio-electrical extraction infrastructure tapping into kidnapped adolescents. The clinical residue is not just structural damage from the lair's destruction but **unknown chemical and bio-electrical exposures** to the rescued teens. No published follow-up bloodwork; no oncology surveillance protocol established.
- **Asgardian relic exposure (Ahmed run):** an artifact of non-terrestrial provenance interacts with the local environment. The neighborhood is exposed to forms of radiation or energy with no terrestrial dosimetry framework.
- **Hydra-era materials:** during occupation, Hydra deployed weaponized tech, surveillance hardware, and chemical crowd-control agents. Post-occupation cleanup is not depicted; residue is implicit.
- **Stormranger debris:** nanite/symbiotic-armor fragments dispersed in residential and commercial blocks. Long-tail behavior of such material is unknown to in-universe medicine.

*Clinical impact:* the subject carries a **toxic burden that is officially unmeasured**. This produces a particular kind of medical anxiety — *the things we cannot name are likely already in us* — that the record does not voice but the behavior reflects: a wary relationship with the waterfront, a tendency to site celebrations *away* from the industrial edge, the unspoken preference for the mosque-and-school inland corridor as the "clean" heart of the body.

### D. Acute Traumatic Injuries (Itemized)

A non-exhaustive ledger of recorded structural trauma:

- **Circle Q:** robbed, vandalized, partially destroyed, used as a battleground, used as a shrine. The single most-injured building in the subject's body. Bruno's family business absorbs the bulk of cumulative trauma because it sits at the geographic and narrative pivot point.
- **Coles Academic High:** repeated lockdowns, structural damage from at least one super-tier event, evacuated multiple times, used as a triage point during the Last Days arc.
- **Khan residence:** windows broken, exterior damage, repeatedly the locus of family-level trauma absorbed by the structure.
- **Mosque (Islamic Masjid):** depicted with security upgrades implying a history of incidents — reinforced door hardware, a camera at the entryway, a sign-in protocol during high-tension periods. The structural body of the mosque is *fortified by accretion*, layer by layer of post-incident hardening, the way human bone remodels around microfractures.
- **Bodega and small-business strip:** glass replacement is a recurring background event. The neighborhood's glaziers, if depicted, would be among the most overworked tradespeople in the city.
- **Streets and curbs:** repeated superhuman-event cratering, partially backfilled, never fully resurfaced.
- **Light-rail platform damage:** at least one panel-confirmed incident.

*Clinical impact:* the body is **scarred in a distributed pattern**, with the highest scar density concentrated on a few overworked organs (Circle Q, Coles, the Khan block). There is no equivalent of Damage Control providing reconstructive surgery; recovery is by **scarring rather than regeneration** — the building gets a patch, not a rebuild. The aesthetic of "patched" then becomes identity, which is reaction-formation at the somatic level.

### E. Disparity in Superhuman-Event Triage

A condition deserving its own line. Manhattan, when struck by a Chitauri-grade event, receives federal-tier reconstruction, insurance underwriting at scale, and Damage Control's full attention. Greenville, when struck by Inventor-grade or Stormranger-grade events, receives **residents with brooms**.

- No federal disaster declaration is depicted for any of the published superhuman-collateral events at Greenville scale.
- No Damage Control crews are shown clearing rubble in Greenville with the speed and apparatus seen in Manhattan tie-ins.
- Insurance arc is not depicted because the implicit answer is *underinsured or uninsured*.

*Clinical impact:* this is **medical triage racism and triage classism** rendered as infrastructure. The neighborhood's body heals by self-suture. The psychological consequence is the durable expectation that **external help is a fiction**, which calcifies the avoidant-features attachment style described in the psychological workup.

---

## III. SUBSTANCES

The published record is, as noted in the shared assessment, restrained on intoxicants. This restraint is itself diagnostic.

### A. What IS depicted

- **Caffeine** in all its working-class registers: bodega drip coffee, chai at the mosque and at home, gas-station coffee from Bruno's, late-night student energy drinks. This is the neighborhood's actual operating substance. Consumption is heavy, normalized, intergenerational.
- **Sugar:** mithai at weddings and milestones, gas-station candy, the sugar-glazed pastries of the Pakistani bakeries, the Dominican repostería. A sweet tooth runs across cultural lines.
- **Tobacco and hookah:** background presence, primarily in the older-adult male social spaces (specific cafés, the corner outside certain establishments). Vaping among the teenage cohort is present but de-emphasized.
- **Halal meat and the entire culinary apparatus** of the local diet, which functions both as nutrition and as a daily ritual of cultural assertion.

### B. What is conspicuously ABSENT

- **No opioid arc.** Given the demographic and economic profile, the actuarial expectation in a real Hudson County neighborhood would include a depicted opioid presence. The record's silence is an authorial choice, not a clinical absence. *Inferred reality:* an opioid presence exists, is felt in the family histories of secondary characters never given panel time, and is metabolized through the mosque and family networks rather than through formal addiction medicine.
- **No alcohol arc of significance.** A Muslim-plurality neighborhood with significant non-Muslim populations would in reality show the usual range; the record under-depicts both adult drinking and adolescent experimentation.
- **No cannabis arc.** Notable in a post-legalization New Jersey. Inferred to be present, normalized, and unremarked.

*Clinical impact:* the silence around the harder substance histories means the neighborhood **carries unspoken bereavements**. Every community of this profile has overdose dead. The mosque has prayed over them; the murals do not name them. This is part of the under-naming pattern — grief held but not catalogued.

### C. The neighborhood's true intoxicant

**Civic gossip** functions pharmacologically: rapid uptake at the bodega counter and mosque foyer, dose-dependent mood effects, tolerance build-up, mild withdrawal syndromes when residents move away. It is the substance that bonds the body to itself.

---

## IV. TRANSFORMATIONS

### A. The Polymorphic Adolescent Embedding

The single most consequential somatic event in the subject's history is the **embedding of an Inhuman polymorphic adolescent within its tissue** — the activation of Kamala Khan as Ms. Marvel, and the subsequent permanent residence of a shape-shifting superhuman within the everyday body of the neighborhood.

This is, in medical terms, a kind of **benign symbiotic graft**. Most communities reject superhumans — Manhattan tolerates them at a celebrity distance; Hell's Kitchen mythologizes them in noir; mutant communities cluster defensively. Greenville **integrated** the graft.

- Civilians wave at her from stoops.
- Aunties pack her food.
- The Circle Q is her de facto safehouse.
- Coles knows and does not formalize the knowing.
- The mosque accommodates her schedule.

This integration is itself a clinical accomplishment. The neighborhood developed **immunological tolerance** to superhuman presence without losing immunological competence against superhuman threat. Compare again to Manhattan and the Fantastic Four: warmer here, less spectacularized, more familial. The difference is that Greenville **does not perform** its superhuman — it absorbs her into the daily metabolism.

### B. The Bereavement / Necrotic Phase (2023)

The Death of Ms. Marvel triggered the most acute affective episode in the record. Somatically:

- The Circle Q acquired a **shrine layer** — candles, flowers, drawings from Coles students, a thickening of the building's exterior into reliquary.
- **Murals** bloomed on multiple walls within days; the neighborhood's graffiti immune response converted grief into pigment.
- The mosque hosted janazah-coded ritual and overflow gatherings.
- Foot traffic patterns shifted toward sites of memorial; the body **circulated differently** for weeks.

*Clinical impact:* this was the body's first published encounter with a death that mattered to it at the structural level. The neighborhood metabolized it through ritual and public art rather than through clinical bereavement services (which, again, are not depicted as available). The grief work was **complete enough to function, incomplete enough to scar**.

### C. The Resurrection / Re-graft Phase

When Kamala returned (in altered form, post-mutant retcon), the neighborhood had to perform the unusual somatic work of **un-grieving**. The murals are not painted over — the record retains them. The shrine is not dismantled — it transitions. This is the equivalent of a graft that died and was successfully reattached: the scar tissue remains, and the body now contains the memory of having lost her even though she is back.

### D. Hydra Occupation as Acute Systemic Infection

The Secret Empire arc functions clinically as a **systemic fascist infection** of the body. Symptoms:

- Loss of self-governance (immune dysregulation).
- Collaborator emergence (autoimmune phenomena — the body attacking parts of itself; the Josh Richardson arc is the textbook example).
- Sheltering of resistance (lymphatic hardening — the mutual-aid network upgraded to clandestine cell structure).
- Post-infection convalescence (depicted briefly; long-tail psychological residue under-depicted but present).

The neighborhood survived the infection but acquired **autoimmune memory**: a sharpened ability to recognize fascist-pattern recruitment in subsequent threats, paired with a sharpened wariness of its own collaborator-prone subgroups.

### E. Stormranger and the Microscopic-Foreign-Body Event

Nanite armor disperses in the body. The neighborhood handles the event without external assistance. Inferred long-tail: trace nanite presence in soil, plumbing, dust. No surveillance program exists.

---

## V. DISABILITIES AND IMPAIRMENTS (Structural)

The neighborhood-body lives with several functional impairments treated as baseline:

- **Reduced ADA mobility access** — older curb cuts, brownstone stoops without ramps, mosque entries with stairs. Aging residents and disabled residents work around this with community assistance, which is a form of compensation, not accommodation.
- **Limited acute-care capacity** — no Level I trauma center inside the subject's geographic body; emergency transport must cross to Newark or Manhattan for the most serious cases. The body's **golden hour is borrowed**.
- **Mental-health under-resourcing** — culturally competent providers are scarce relative to need; mosque-based pastoral counseling and family networks substitute. This is functional until it is not.
- **Pharmacy access** — present, but the small independent pharmacies are economically squeezed by chain encroachment.
- **Pediatric specialist access** — limited locally; families travel for serious care.

These are not "the neighborhood's disabilities" so much as the **disabilities imposed on the neighborhood by under-resourcing**. The distinction matters: the body did not become disabled, it was disabled.

---

## VI. SURGERIES (Civic / Built-Environment Interventions)

Treating major civic interventions as surgical procedures:

- **Attempted hostile surgery — the Hope Yards Development Initiative (Chuck Worthy):** a proposed forced amputation and replacement of the Greenville heart with a luxury-grafted simulacrum. The body refused consent. The procedure was halted at the consultation stage by organized civic confrontation. *Clinical impact:* the neighborhood discovered that the surgeons most likely to operate on it without consent were not supervillains but developers — a permanent shift in the body's threat model.
- **Self-performed reconstructive work:** every post-event rebuild of the Circle Q, the Khan residence, the school gym, the storefronts. The neighborhood is its own field surgeon, with all the limits that implies.
- **Mosque hardening:** the accretive security upgrades function as a series of small prophylactic surgeries against future incidents.
- **Implied light-rail extensions and station upgrades:** depicted in background panels in later runs; the body slowly receiving better-perfused vasculature in its more-visible districts while the deeper interior remains undertreated.

---

## VII. PSYCHOLOGICAL IMPACT OF THE MEDICAL HISTORY

Aggregating the somatic record, the psychological consequences are coherent and predictable:

1. **High pain tolerance.** A body that has been hurt repeatedly and patched by its own residents stops registering low-grade pain as remarkable. This is adaptive in the short run, pathogenic in the long — chronic harms fail to mobilize response.
2. **Low trust in external care systems.** The disparity in superhuman-event triage and the absence of federal recovery resources have trained the body to expect abandonment. Civic muscle compensates; civic resentment accumulates.
3. **Strong somatic identification with specific organs.** The Circle Q, the mosque, Coles, the Khan block are *load-bearing* psychologically. Damage to them is felt as injury-to-self in a way that damage to anonymous infrastructure is not. This is why the post-Kamala shrine clustered at the Circle Q rather than at, say, the light-rail station — the body knows which of its organs hold meaning.
4. **Under-naming of structural harm.** Brownfield exposure, opioid presence, mental-health unmet need — the body declines to articulate these because articulation has historically not produced redress. Silence is a learned response, not a baseline.
5. **Ritualization of recovery.** Public art, communal meals, mosque-coordinated convalescence, civic gossip as informational immune response. The neighborhood heals **liturgically**, and this works for grief better than for toxicology.
6. **Wariness of the waterfront.** A spatial somatization. The body knows where its liver is and does not picnic there.
7. **Accretive hardening rather than systemic reform.** Each incident produces a small local fortification — a camera, a reinforced door, a community watch — rather than a structural overhaul. The body becomes a palimpsest of small defenses, none individually sufficient.

---

## VIII. CLINICAL SUMMARY

The subject presents as a community-body with a **century-deep substrate of industrial and economic insult**, a **decade-acute layer of superhuman-collateral injury**, an **embedded benign superhuman graft**, a **recent bereavement-and-resurrection cycle**, and a **chronic, untreated, but socially-compensated mental-health and toxic-exposure burden**. Mortality is not elevated relative to peer neighborhoods; morbidity is widely distributed and broadly under-diagnosed. Prognosis is **guarded but stable** so long as the mutual-aid networks remain intact and the gentrification pressure does not achieve what supervillains could not.

The defining medical finding: **this is a body that has never received the standard of care its injuries warranted, and that has, in compensation, learned to be its own physician — competently, lovingly, and incompletely.**


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — JERSEY CITY NEIGHBORHOOD (Greenville / 616)

*Methodological preface.* A neighborhood's "body" is the aggregate of its built fabric, its weather-on-asphalt, its crowd-flows, its acoustic signature, and the synchronized micro-behaviors of its residents in shared space. What follows treats the panels of the Wilson, Ahmed, and adjacent runs as surveillance feeds: every recurring storefront pose, every crowd-gait at 7:42 a.m. on Kennedy Boulevard, every shrug at a passing siren, is somatic data. The Atlas catalogs the subject as a living organism with reproducible postural defaults, characteristic tics, sleep architecture, feeding cycles, intimacy patterns, and state-dependent shifts.

---

## I. BASELINE POSTURE & STANDING ARCHITECTURE

The neighborhood at rest stands **slightly hunched, weight on the back foot, hands in pockets.** This is observable in the consistent way Greenville is drawn at street level: awnings sag a few degrees off true; the Circle Q's signage tilts perceptibly left; brownstone stoops are inhabited rather than ascended — bodies sit *on* them rather than pass *over* them. The architectural posture is **occupied lean**, not parade-ground vertical.

Sidewalk-width is functionally narrowed by stoop-sitters, milk-crate chess setups, folding chairs outside the halal cart, and the perennial sandwich-board for Bruno's specials. Pedestrians flow in a **single-file negotiation pattern** rather than the two-abreast Manhattan grid. This produces a characteristic neighborhood **micro-gait**: short stride, lateral shoulder-turn every six to eight paces to pass, frequent eye contact, frequent nodded greeting. The gait is **socially permeable** — interrupted easily, resumed easily.

Standing groups cluster in **threes and fours**, never twos. Pairs are read as conversations-in-progress; trios are the social default. The mosque foyer, the bodega counter, the Coles front steps, and the Khan stoop all reliably hold trios. A solitary standing figure on a Greenville sidewalk is a **somatic anomaly** the neighborhood notices within seconds — heads turn from windows, the bodega cat repositions.

---

## II. GAIT, FLOW, AND CIRCADIAN MOVEMENT

The neighborhood's **diurnal kinetics** follow a reproducible four-phase cycle:

- **05:15–07:00 — Pre-commute hush.** Movement is sparse, weighted, slow. The fajr call shifts foot-traffic toward the masjid; bakery and bodega shutters roll up in a staggered sequence west-to-east along the avenue. The neighborhood's pulse rate, measured in footfalls-per-minute on the main commercial corridor, is at its lowest.
- **07:00–09:00 — Commuter extraction.** The PATH/light-rail siphon. Bodies move with **directional uniformity** toward stations; gait lengthens, phone-screens illuminate faces, coffee cups establish a forearm-perpendicular hand position. This is the only window in the day when the neighborhood walks like Manhattan walks. Even so, the gait retains a **lateral-yield habit** — Jersey commuters step aside for each other; Manhattan commuters do not. This persists as a tell when Greenville residents are observed across the river.
- **09:00–14:30 — Resident-economy idle.** Movement is errand-shaped: short loops between bodega, halal cart, school pickup line, mosque, pharmacy, laundromat. Strides are shorter; the **dwelling-pause** (the stationary 30–90 second conversation in mid-sidewalk) reappears as a dominant feature. Body language is **leaned-in, hip-cocked, weight on one leg.**
- **14:30–17:00 — School disgorgement.** Coles Academic and the lower schools release; the somatic profile shifts to **adolescent kinetic noise** — backpack-swing, shoulder-check rough-housing, the loitering arc that pulls teen clusters toward the Circle Q within twelve to eighteen minutes of dismissal bell.
- **17:00–20:30 — Re-aggregation.** Commuters return. Gait is **heavier, slower, shoulders rolled forward**, but greetings re-fire. The bodega bell rings at a measurable peak between 18:10 and 19:00.
- **20:30–23:30 — Stoop and screen.** Residents externalize onto stoops, fire escapes, and rolled-down car windows. Movement minimizes; sound localizes (TVs through open windows, the masjid's late prayer dispersal, teenagers' Bluetooth speakers).
- **23:30–05:15 — Sleep architecture (collective).** The neighborhood does not fully sleep. There is a baseline insomniac residue — the night-shift nurse walking from the jitney stop, the bodega's 24-hour shift change at 02:00, the periodic siren from Bayonne direction. Collective REM, if such a thing can be inferred from quietness-density, peaks around 03:40–04:30. This is the only time the neighborhood is **somatically still.**

---

## III. HANDS, FACE, AND MICRO-EXPRESSION

**Hand patterns:**
- *Bodega counter hand.* Resting palm-down on the counter glass, fingers slightly splayed, thumb tapping at intervals of two to four seconds during conversation. Universal across Bruno's customers in published panels.
- *Stoop hand.* One hand cradling a paper cup (chai, coffee, juice); the other gestures in arcs no wider than the shoulders. Greenville does not gesticulate beyond its own silhouette — a tight-radius habit consistent with crowded sidewalk evolution.
- *Mosque foyer hand.* Both hands clasped at the navel, or one hand to the heart in greeting (the *salaam* gesture), a slight forward bow of seven to ten degrees. Repeated dozens of times per Friday in the published record.
- *Worry-hand.* When the neighborhood is stressed (Inventor disappearances, Hydra occupation, the death-of-Kamala bereavement), hands migrate to **face and neck** — palm to cheek, fingers to mouth, the back of the hand to the forehead. Women elders are drawn with the *aanchal* (scarf-edge) pressed to the mouth; men with the open palm flat across the lower face.

**Facial defaults:**
- *Resting Greenville face* is **mildly amused, eyes slightly narrowed, mouth flat with a one-degree upward asymmetry on the left.** This is the dryness, the in-on-the-joke quality. It is *not* the Manhattan resting-neutral (vigilant, foreshortened) nor the suburban resting-pleasant (open-mouth half-smile). It is **the face of someone waiting for the punchline they already wrote.**
- *Eyebrow tells.* A single raised eyebrow is the neighborhood's most economical signal — used at supervillain debris, at gentrifier real-estate signage, at a tourist asking directions to Hoboken. The eyebrow does not return to baseline immediately; it lingers a half-second, a held judgment.
- *Eye-contact economy.* Greenville makes brief, warm, frequent eye contact at peer-distance (under twelve feet); breaks contact with authority figures (cops, suits, federal agents) at the **mid-sentence beat** — a learned avoidance that reads as deference but functions as withholding.

**Micro-tics observed across the record:**
- The **shoulder shrug-with-half-smile** when something inexplicable occurs (an Asgardian artifact in the marina, Ms. Marvel embiggening on the rooftop) — the city's signature shrug at the impossible.
- The **two-finger wave** from stoops at passing residents, never raised above the chest.
- The **chin-lift greeting** between teenagers, exclusively male, exclusively under twenty-two.
- The **head-tilt of skepticism** when an outsider speaks — a four-to-six degree lateral tilt held for the duration of the outsider's pitch.

---

## IV. VOICE, ACOUSTICS, AND BREATH

The neighborhood **breathes audibly** in a way Manhattan does not. The acoustic baseline is layered: HVAC hum from undermaintained units (a slightly off-pitch drone, more B-flat than the Manhattan A), bodega refrigerator compressors, the PATH rumble at predictable intervals, gulls from the waterfront, the dispersed adhan five times daily, distant Spanish-language radio, the bell at Bruno's, basketball-on-asphalt from the courts behind Coles. Crucially, **none of these sounds is layered loudly enough to mask conversation at three feet.** The acoustic body is **dense but talk-permeable**.

**Voice patterns:**
- The neighborhood **code-switches fluidly between five or six registers within a single block**: Urdu/English Khan-family register, Bruno's flat Jersey-accented English, Sheikh Abdullah's measured pulpit cadence, the Spanish of the Dominican grocer two doors down, the Italian-American holdovers' shortened vowels, the teenage internet-inflected patois. The somatic correlate is **rapid lingual repositioning** — residents' jaw and tongue posture re-set in mid-sentence.
- **Volume** is moderate. The neighborhood does not shout to be heard the way midtown does; it leans in. This produces a characteristic **forward head-carriage** in conversation, four to seven degrees of cervical flexion.
- **Laughter** is plentiful, mid-pitched, and short-burst. The belly laugh is rare; the **two-syllable dry exhale-laugh** is the neighborhood's dominant amusement vocalization.

Under stress the voice profile shifts: **pitch lowers, cadence slows, sentences shorten.** Crowd-volume during the Inventor crisis and the post-Kamala bereavement is documented as *quieter than baseline*, not louder. This is a hallmark of trauma-experienced communities: noise during grief reads as performance; silence as truth.

---

## V. GROOMING, DRESS, AND SURFACE PRESENTATION

The neighborhood's **dermal layer** — its painted facades, awnings, shutters, signage — is groomed inconsistently. Bruno's storefront is swept twice daily, the bodega glass cleaned at shift change. The mosque is immaculate within, weathered without (an inversion of evangelical-American practice). Brownstone stoops are scrubbed Saturday mornings by older residents in a ritual older than any of the writers; the sidewalk in front of one's house is **dermatologically one's own**.

Civic graffiti operates as the neighborhood's **tattoo culture**: meaningful, gendered, generational, semi-permitted. The murals are not buffed quickly; the tags are. There is a clear in-group/out-group distinction in what is allowed to remain on the skin.

Dress on residents is **layered, modest, and unfussy.** The mosque-going population's *shalwar kameez* and *thobe* coexist with hijab-and-jeans, with Coles uniforms, with Devils jerseys, with bodega-worker hoodies, with the construction-trades Carhartt of the Italian-American old guard. There is no single neighborhood dress code; the *code is variety itself*, and outsiders attempting to read a single dress-cue (the well-meaning federal agent in *Magnificent*, e.g.) are visibly miscalibrated.

**Hair, skin, scent:** the neighborhood smells, across the day, of fryer oil at the halal cart, cardamom from the Khan kitchen exhaust, diesel at the PATH stairwell, sea-rot at the waterfront, baking sugar from the Dominican bakery on the south end, and — Friday afternoons — *attar* drifting from the mosque parking lot. This olfactory signature is one of the most stable somatic features of the subject across writers.

---

## VI. EATING, FEEDING, AND ORAL HABIT

The neighborhood eats **constantly, communally, and on its feet.** Sit-down meals are reserved for home tables (the Khan kitchen, the Carelli back room, the iftar gatherings during Ramadan); the public eating posture is **standing, paper-bag-in-hand, second hand free for conversation.**

- **Bodega feeding** — the Circle Q bacon-egg-and-cheese (or the halal-modified version) is the neighborhood's morning communion. Hand-to-mouth cycle: six to eight seconds per bite; ninety seconds to clear; foil retained as napkin.
- **Halal-cart lunch** — rice plate consumed standing, fork in right hand, hot sauce ritualized.
- **Chai/coffee** — held continuously between meals. The neighborhood's hand is rarely empty of a cup between 06:30 and 14:00.
- **Sweet hour** — Dominican bakery output peaks at 15:00, Pakistani sweets at 16:30, both consumed walking.
- **Ramadan inversion** — the most somatically remarkable annual rhythm. The neighborhood's eating cycle inverts: daylight quiet, post-maghrib explosion of communal feeding, late-night activity stretching to suhoor. Coles' lunchroom adjusts informally; Bruno's stays open later; the masjid feeds hundreds. This **annual circadian re-architecture** is one of the most distinctive somatic facts about Greenville and one of the more accurate Wilson-era depictions.

The neighborhood does not snack alone in public; solo eating reads as **distress** and draws stoop-glances.

---

## VII. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

Collective sleep is **fragmented, plural, and economically determined.** The neighborhood contains:
- The early-rise shift (mosque-aligned and trades-aligned, 04:30–05:30 wake).
- The commuter shift (05:30–07:00 wake).
- The school shift (06:30–07:30 wake, with adolescent resistance).
- The service-economy shift (variable; night cleaners returning at 02:00–04:00).
- The teen nocturne (asleep 01:00–10:00 on weekends, parental friction documented).

There is **no hour in which the entire neighborhood sleeps simultaneously.** This is the somatic basis for its perpetual semi-alertness — the body is never fully unconscious, which contributes to its calm under cosmic-tier threat (the neighborhood is *already* awake when the sky cracks).

REM-density windows are 02:30–05:00 in summer, 03:00–05:30 in winter. The bodega's quietest five minutes are reliably 03:50–03:55 — the neighborhood's diastole.

---

## VIII. SEXUAL AND INTIMATE PATTERNS

The published record is appropriately oblique here, but somatic inference is possible. The neighborhood's intimacy is **domestic, kin-structured, and largely interior.** Public displays are modest: the brief hand-touch at the mosque steps between spouses; the teenage hand-hold at the marina under a specific lamp-post the panels have rendered three times; the Aamir-Tyesha post-wedding domesticity coded through threshold and kitchen rather than bedroom.

Adolescent romantic geography concentrates at:
- The Coles back stairwell.
- The Liberty State Park southern picnic tables.
- The bodega's second aisle (the snack aisle is the unofficial flirtation corridor).
- The pier railings just south of the marina.

The neighborhood's **erotic somatic** is **anticipatory rather than consummated** — long looks, prolonged greetings, the lingering forearm-touch between elder women friends, the masculine half-hug-and-back-pat. The published record's restraint is itself accurate to a community whose dominant religious and cultural strands prefer private intimacy.

What the record *does* depict explicitly: the **familial physical vocabulary** of the Khan household — Yusuf's hand on Kamala's shoulder, Muneeba's palm to her daughter's cheek, Aamir's headlock-affection toward Kamala — and the **chosen-family physical vocabulary** of Kamala-Bruno-Nakia: the side-hug, the bicep-grab in conversation, the head-on-shoulder during exhaustion. These templates propagate outward; the neighborhood's adolescents touch each other the way the lead trio does.

---

## IX. STATE-DEPENDENT SHIFTS

### A. Calm (baseline)
Posture loose, gait permeable, eye contact frequent, voice mid-volume, hands occupied with cups or phones, micro-laughter dispersed every forty to ninety seconds at peer-density. The neighborhood at calm is **kinetically generous** — it gives sidewalk, gives time, gives "you good?"

### B. Stress (acute — Inventor crisis, missing teens, Stormranger threat)
- Gait **shortens and speeds** without losing lateral-yield.
- Trios condense to **dyads of urgent purpose.**
- Bodega counter-time **drops by half**; transactions become curt but not cold.
- Stoop occupancy **rises** — elders deploy as passive surveillance.
- Phone-checking frequency **triples**.
- The shrug-with-half-smile **disappears**; the eyebrow-raise persists.
- Voice pitch **drops** by a measurable third; laughter near-extinct.
- Mosque attendance at non-prayer hours **increases**; the foyer becomes operational HQ.

### C. Threat (occupation, fascist control, supervillain attack)
- The neighborhood **gets quieter, not louder.**
- Window shades close on a **block-wave pattern** — observable in the Hydra arc.
- Stoop activity **migrates indoors**, but is replaced by **rooftop and fire-escape watching** — the neighborhood's eyes go up.
- Movement becomes **patterned and known-route only**; no one takes new shortcuts.
- Adolescents are **physically gathered inward** — the somatic version of the mama-cat carry. Coles attendance becomes a daily roll-call.
- The bodega's **door-bell rings less but stays-open hours extend** — Bruno's somatic correlate of the lighthouse principle.
- Hand-to-hand contact within trusted units **increases**: more touching of shoulders, more hugs at greeting and parting, more hand-holding among elder women walking together.

### D. Intimacy (collective — wedding, Ramadan, public mourning)
- Posture **opens**: shoulders back, chest forward, hands away from pockets.
- The trios become **quartets and quintets** — the cluster size expands.
- Eye contact **lengthens**.
- Voice **rises in pitch but not volume**; the register becomes warm-treble.
- Eating becomes **continuous and shared from common plates** — the Aamir wedding scenes, the iftar tables, the post-funeral langar at the masjid.
- Touch becomes **prolonged, palmar, and reciprocated** — embraces hold for a count of four to six rather than the baseline one to two.
- Crying is **permitted in public**, especially at the mosque steps and on the Circle Q sidewalk — the two civic sites where collective tears are coded as appropriate rather than alarming.

### E. Grief (specific — death of Ms. Marvel, 2023)
The most somatically distinct state in the record.
- **Murals proliferate** within seventy-two hours — the dermal layer absorbs the loss.
- The Circle Q sidewalk becomes a **shrine**: candles in the daytime (unusual), flowers, taped photographs, handwritten Urdu and English notes. The somatic geometry is **kneeling rather than standing** — the neighborhood is, for the first time in the published record, drawn *on its knees* in significant numbers.
- Stoop-sitting **lengthens to silent durations** — figures depicted sitting without speaking for full panels, the conversational hum of the neighborhood gone temporarily mute.
- Eating **decreases** publicly; communal cooking *increases* privately — food moves into homes in covered dishes rather than onto sidewalks.
- The mosque's foyer is **drawn fuller** at non-prayer times than at prayer times — a documented inversion.
- The neighborhood's **breath is held** — the acoustic baseline thins; the panels' background detail simplifies; even the gulls are absent from waterfront frames for two issues. This is, somatically, the closest the subject comes to **collapse**, and it does not collapse. It mourns and resumes — slower, dimmer, but resumed.

### F. Joy (peer-tier, non-cosmic — local wins, Coles team victories, Eid, neighborhood weddings)
- Gait **bounces**; the lateral-yield becomes a **lateral-dance**, residents sidestep each other with theatrical flourish.
- The two-syllable dry laugh becomes a **full belly laugh**, briefly.
- Stoops fill **beyond capacity**; chairs are dragged out.
- Music plays from **multiple windows simultaneously, in different genres, without conflict** — the somatic signature of pluralist celebration.
- Children are **lifted** — onto shoulders, onto stoop railings, onto adults' laps — the only state in which the neighborhood reliably elevates its smallest bodies above adult eye-level.

---

## X. SOMATIC SIGNATURES — THE IDENTIFYING TELLS

If the file is to be useful for **recognition** — distinguishing this neighborhood from any other in the Marvel record — the following micro-features are diagnostic:

1. **The left-tilted half-amused mouth at rest.** Not Hell's Kitchen's grim flat-line, not the Bronx's open laugh-ready, not the Upper West Side's pleasant-neutral.
2. **The lateral-yield gait.** Persists even when residents are across the river — a Greenville body in Manhattan still steps aside.
3. **The trio default in public standing groups.**
4. **The shrug-with-half-smile at the impossible.**
5. **The single raised eyebrow at the gentrifier's sign.**
6. **The forward head-carriage in conversation** (lean-in, not project-out).
7. **The acoustic permeability** — sound layered but never masking talk.
8. **The dermal inversion at the mosque** (immaculate within, weathered without).
9. **The Ramadan circadian flip.**
10. **The kneeling-at-the-Circle-Q posture of acute collective grief** — a body-shape unique in the record to this neighborhood at this moment.
11. **The two-finger chest-height wave from stoops.**
12. **The 03:50–03:55 diastole** — the five-minute window of full somatic stillness, never longer.

---

*Atlas closes here; the body it describes does not. The neighborhood's somatic signature is, finally, that of an organism* **chronically half-awake, half-amused, half-bent toward its own** — *a body that has learned to carry itself, and to carry its dead, without waiting to be carried.*


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS
## Subject: Jersey City Neighborhood (Greenville, Marvel-616)

---

## I. CLASSIFICATION OF ATTACHMENT STYLE

The subject presents, in the language of adult attachment research applied at collective scale, as **earned-secure with pronounced avoidant features directed selectively at extra-local authority**. The qualifier *earned* is essential: this is not the secure attachment of a population raised in conditions of consistent institutional care. It is the secure attachment of a population that **built its own holding environment** after discovering, repeatedly, that the larger systems would not provide one. The internal working model can be paraphrased: *People who live here will show up. People who do not live here may show up, but plan as if they will not.*

This is structurally identical to the attachment profile observed in adult children of unreliable caregivers who have successfully constituted chosen-family networks in adulthood — high intra-network trust, calibrated extra-network skepticism, and a capacity to extend provisional trust to outsiders who pass a recurring proof-of-presence test. The neighborhood is not closed; it is *probationary*.

Crucially, the subject does **not** display the disorganized attachment one would predict from its objective trauma load (industrial abandonment, post-9/11 surveillance, repeated superhuman collateral, gentrification pressure). The protective factors — the mosque, the dense bodega-stoop-school sociality, the intergenerational mentorship infrastructure, the unusual density of religiously-grounded ethical frameworks across multiple traditions cohabiting without forced syncretism — have absorbed what could have produced fragmentation and metabolized it into coherence.

---

## II. ORIGINS OF THE STYLE

Four etiological strata can be identified in the record:

**Stratum 1 — Post-industrial abandonment (pre-textual, inferred from environment).** The neighborhood's built tissue — the brownfield waterfront, the deferred-maintenance corridors, the chronic Coles HVAC failures, the taped bodega glass — encodes a memory of being a place that *made things for an economy that left*. The attachment legacy of being made redundant by capital is a foundational distrust of institutions that arrive promising development. This is the deepest layer, the equivalent of early-childhood schema: by the time the published record begins, this lesson is preconscious.

**Stratum 2 — Post-9/11 surveillance and the Aamir detention substrate.** The Wilson-run sequences in which Aamir Khan is detained without charge, the ambient anxiety around the mosque, the casual coding of Muslim residents as security objects — these constitute a more recent, more specific betrayal trauma. It is the source of the neighborhood's **selective avoidance of federal-tier authority** and its instinctive sheltering posture toward its own Muslim residents. The wound is sectoral but it shapes the whole nervous system, because the Khan family is so central to the social graph that what is done to them is felt everywhere.

**Stratum 3 — Superhuman-event triage disparity.** Each Inventor attack, each Hydra occupation, each Stormranger incident, each spillover from a Manhattan crisis arrives, gets resolved, and does not generate the Damage Control response that the same destruction in Midtown would generate. The neighborhood learns, in a Pavlovian register, that *the cavalry comes for Manhattan and the broom comes for us*. This is the source of the avoidant feature: not hostility toward heroes, but a worked-through expectation that praise is for them and cleanup is for us.

**Stratum 4 — The Kamala emergence and the Ms. Marvel iconography.** The most recent and only positive attachment-formative event: a child of the neighborhood became powerful and **did not leave**. She patrolled Greenville. She failed her chemistry homework. She got grounded. The neighborhood watched a superhuman being *remain familial*, and this revised, partially, the avoidant schema toward at least one super-tier figure. The 2023 bereavement was structurally analogous to a community losing a daughter who had stayed, not a celebrity who had visited.

---

## III. HOW THE SUBJECT BONDS

Bonding is **proximal, repetitive, and unceremonious**. The neighborhood does not formalize new relationships through ritual induction; it forms them through *accumulated co-presence in specific micro-locations*. The Circle Q counter is the primary bonding site — Bruno's register is a confessional booth that pretends to be a transaction surface. Secondary bonding sites in descending order of intensity: the mosque foyer (post-prayer, before dispersal); the Khan kitchen (highest-trust tier, family-graduated); the Coles cafeteria and adjacent stoop network; the halal cart line; the PATH platform at commute hours (low-grade ambient solidarity rather than conversation).

The bonding tempo is **slow then total**. A new neighbor exists in a probationary zone for an indeterminate period — months, sometimes years — characterized by polite acknowledgment without invitation. The transition to insider status is rarely marked by a single event; it is marked retroactively, by the recognition that one is now being *asked* for things (a ride, a recommendation, a sign-on to a petition, a plate at iftar). Being asked is the citizenship document. The neighborhood does not say *welcome*; it says *you got a minute?*

Within the bonded zone, the affective register is **dry, teasing, and operationally affectionate**. Verbal warmth is rationed; practical solicitude is unlimited. A resident in distress will receive food, transportation, childcare, and an alibi before they receive a hug. This is not coldness — it is a culture in which **logistics is the language of love**. The hug is implicit in the casserole.

---

## IV. HOW THE SUBJECT DISTRUSTS

Distrust is **layered, signal-driven, and rarely declared aloud**. The neighborhood operates a continuous, low-resolution surveillance of outsiders that bears no resemblance to paranoia and considerable resemblance to a small village's vetting protocols. The signals it reads are:

- **Wardrobe-to-context mismatch.** Anyone overdressed for the block is logged. The Worthy-era developers — their suits, their unscuffed shoes — were identified as threats before they opened their mouths.
- **Map-checking behavior.** Residents know their way; visitors who know their way too well (real estate scouts, undercover agents) read as wrong in a different and more alarming register.
- **The Manhattan accent of presumption.** Not the geographic accent; the tonal one — the assumption that one's time is more valuable than the counter clerk's. Bruno's deadpan is partly a diagnostic instrument calibrated to this frequency.
- **Photography without permission.** Particularly of the mosque, particularly of children. Triggers immediate, quiet, coordinated counter-observation.
- **The arrival of forms.** Federal forms, developer forms, survey forms. The neighborhood's paperwork-allergy is not illiteracy; it is correctly learned suspicion that documentation precedes displacement.

Distrust is not expressed through confrontation in the first instance. It is expressed through **withdrawal of information** — the suddenly vague directions, the conveniently absent owner, the rescheduled appointment, the polite *I don't know him* about someone everyone knows. The neighborhood gaslights its predators with a smile. This is a learned, ancient defensive technology of communities under surveillance, and Greenville deploys it without thinking.

Distrust escalates from informational withdrawal to **physical convergence** (the small group that materializes when a stranger lingers too long near a child), and only then to verbal confrontation or, in extremity, to the calling of the local hero. Police-equivalent escalation is rare and reluctant, and it is notable how seldom in the record the neighborhood resolves a problem through arrest.

---

## V. HOW THE SUBJECT IS BETRAYED — AND HOW IT BETRAYS

The neighborhood has been betrayed at every scale represented in canon, and its responses cluster into a recognizable pattern.

**By institutions:** The wound is absorbed without dramatic protest and then encoded into permanent operational caution. The Aamir detention did not produce a riot; it produced a hardened mosque security culture, a more careful intake of strangers asking about congregants, and an intergenerational transfer of the specific knowledge of *which questions from authorities precede which harms*. The neighborhood does not forgive the betraying institution; it simply removes that institution from its functional trust map and routes around it.

**By developers:** Treated as a slow predation rather than a personal betrayal, which is correct. The response is civic — town halls, organizing, the Wilson-run Discordians/Hope Yards arc's mobilizations — and it is notable that it produced **coalition behavior across demographic lines that elsewhere in the Marvel record do not coalition easily**. Shared threat to place overrides intra-community friction.

**By its own (Hydra collaborators, the Worthy-allied locals):** This is where the neighborhood's response is least mature and most revealing. In-group betrayal triggers **splitting** — the temporary cleaving of the community into good-Jersey and bad-Jersey, the scapegoating of collaborators in language that sometimes elides the systemic pressures (economic precarity, fear) that produced the collaboration. The record (Josh Richardson's arc particularly) does not let the neighborhood off the hook here. Internal betrayal is the wound the subject metabolizes worst, because the entire architecture of self assumes *we take care of our own*, and the betrayer falsifies the premise.

Repair from in-group betrayal, when it occurs in the record, is slow, conditional, and mediated by elders — Sheikh Abdullah, the older Khan generation, certain bodega-owning patriarchs and matriarchs whose authority is convening rather than executive. Repair requires the betrayer to have **stayed** (those who left are not repaired with; they are simply written out) and to have submitted to a probationary re-entry that is, in its tempo, similar to the original outsider-to-insider transition but with a permanent asterisk.

**How the subject betrays:** The neighborhood's own betrayals are almost exclusively **betrayals by silence** — the failure to name Islamophobic incidents publicly when naming would be costly, the under-protection of residents whose marginalization sits within the neighborhood (queer kids in religiously conservative families, women in domestic distress whose privacy norms protect their abusers, undocumented residents whose status complicates mobilization). These are not active betrayals; they are the negative space of a mutual-aid culture whose mechanisms are tuned to legible, communal crises and not to private ones. The subject under-recognizes this failure mode, and the record does not let it off the hook either, though it treats the failure with more compassion than the active collaboration.

---

## VI. HOW THE SUBJECT REPAIRS

Repair is **public, ritualized, and food-mediated**. The neighborhood does not have a therapeutic vocabulary; it has a meals vocabulary. After every major rupture — the Inventor arc's recovered children, the Last Days passage, the Hydra retreat, the Kamala bereavement — the response is convergence in a shared eating space and the production of more food than is necessary. The excess is the message: *we are not rationing; we have not lost the capacity to give*.

Ritualized repair markers in the record:
- **Murals.** Post-bereavement, post-victory. Public surface as collective journal. The Circle Q wall is the canonical site.
- **The wedding-as-repair.** Aamir's wedding in the Ahmed run functions as a community-wide reaffirmation of continuity after sustained stress.
- **Communal meals at the mosque.** Iftar is the most legible, but unscheduled post-crisis gatherings follow the same template.
- **The reopening of the Circle Q.** Every time it has been damaged, its reopening is treated as a civic milestone. The bodega is not a store; it is a vital organ, and its function is monitored.

What is conspicuously absent: **clinical repair**. Grief counselors do not appear. Trauma-informed institutional response is not depicted at scale. The neighborhood holds its wounds in communal space and does not always notice when an individual wound exceeds the holding capacity of casserole and conversation. This is the under-resourced flank of an otherwise robust repair apparatus.

---

## VII. INTIMACY AND DEPENDENCY

The neighborhood's intimacy style is **high-context and low-disclosure**. Residents know an enormous amount about each other — schedules, family troubles, medical conditions, romantic prospects — through ambient observation rather than confided disclosure. The information flows through what could be called the **mosque-bodega-stoop pipeline**, a triadic gossip infrastructure that is simultaneously a surveillance system, a wellness check, and a social safety net. To be known here is to be cared for and also to be unable to hide.

Dependency is **distributed and reciprocal**. No single relationship in the network bears the full weight of any individual's needs; the load is spread across a redundant graph (your mother, your imam, the bodega owner who fronts you a sandwich, the auntie who watches your sibling, the teacher who calls when you miss class). This is the structural source of the neighborhood's resilience and also the reason individuals who try to extract themselves from the network — for college, for marriage outside, for opportunity — experience the extraction as a partial amputation that the network reciprocally feels. Departure is grieved, sometimes for years, and returnees are received with a complicated mixture of celebration and corrective re-socialization.

Dependency on a single relationship is treated, in the record, as a warning sign. When Bruno's grief in Wakanda isolates him, the narrative reads it as pathology *for this neighborhood specifically*, because solitude is not the cultural baseline. The same isolation in a Hell's Kitchen character would read as routine; in a Greenville character it reads as a crisis requiring intervention.

Romantic and familial intimacy operates within and is shaped by this distributed-dependency culture. Couples are absorbed into the network rather than functioning as private dyads; weddings are civic events; in-laws are inherited as additional load-bearing nodes. The cost is privacy; the benefit is that no marriage fails alone and no parent raises a child alone.

---

## VIII. THE RELATIONAL TEMPLATE — REPEATED ACROSS EVERY RELATIONSHIP

Across every dyad and every interaction the neighborhood participates in — with its residents, with its heroes, with its enemies, with Manhattan, with the federal government, with developers, with the cosmic, with the franchise itself — the same template recurs. It can be stated as a five-beat pattern:

**1. Provisional welcome.** The other is greeted with surface politeness and operational reserve. Tea is offered; trust is not.

**2. Proof through presence.** The other is observed across repeated, low-stakes interactions. Are they here when it rains? Do they remember names? Do they pay their tab? Do they show up when someone's grandmother is in the hospital? The test is duration, not gesture.

**3. Conditional integration.** The other is gradually folded into the dependency graph — asked for favors, included in invitations, given access to the kitchen-tier rather than the counter-tier. Integration is never announced; it is recognized in retrospect.

**4. Tested loyalty under stress.** Crisis arrives — an Inventor, a Hydra, a developer, a bereavement, a wedding logistics catastrophe — and the integrated other's behavior under load is the final calibration. Loyalty here means *staying and being useful*, not *being heroic*. The neighborhood prefers a reliable mediocre helper to a glamorous unreliable one.

**5. Permanent placement, or permanent exile.** After the stress test the other is either embedded for life (and will receive food at their funeral if they die fifty years later) or quietly, conclusively removed from the trust map. There is rarely a third outcome. The neighborhood does not maintain ambiguous relationships at long range; ambiguity is resolved by attrition.

This template applies, with adjustments of tempo and scale, to:
- A new family moving onto the block.
- A new teacher at Coles.
- A new vendor near the halal cart.
- The Champions as an organization.
- The Avengers as an institution (still at beat 2 after a decade — they keep showing up, they have not yet proven presence in the local sense).
- Manhattan as a polity (permanently arrested at beat 1; not because Manhattan has failed the test but because Manhattan has not understood that a test is being administered).
- Hydra (failed beat 4 catastrophically; permanent exile).
- Developers (failed beat 1; never even admitted to the probationary zone).
- Ms. Marvel (the rare case of someone born inside the network at beat 5 from birth, whose loss is felt as the loss of a load-bearing node rather than a celebrity).

The deepest fact about the subject's relational life is that **this template is the same template the neighborhood uses on itself, internally, every day**, and it is the same template by which the neighborhood will eventually evaluate the franchise that contains it: *did Marvel show up, slowly, repeatedly, with food, when no one was watching, for long enough to be asked for a favor?* The neighborhood is, even now, taking notes.


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# DEFENSES & COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS
## Subject: Jersey City Neighborhood (Greenville / Marvel-616)

The defensive architecture of a *place* is not a single ego's set of habits but a **stratified, redundant lattice** distributed across institutions, built surfaces, recurring micro-rituals, and the bodies of individual residents who carry the neighborhood's reflexes. What follows maps that lattice in full: every observable defense in the published record, ranked by primitiveness from the most mature to the most regressed, with the **behavioral signature** by which each is recognized on the page, the **trigger conditions** under which it activates, the **somatic/spatial substrate** it lives in, the **cost** it exacts, and — critically — the **failure modes** under which it stops protecting and starts harming.

---

## I. MATURE DEFENSES (Vaillant Level IV)

These are the load-bearing defenses of the subject. They are the reason the neighborhood is functional rather than merely traumatized.

### 1. Humor — specifically, *deadpan undersell*

The single most pervasive defense in the record. It manifests in at least four distinct registers, each with its own bearer:

- **Bodega-counter deadpan** (Bruno Carrelli's mode): flat affect, dry observation, the refusal to escalate emotional pitch even when an Inhuman teenager has just punched a hole through the ceiling. Behaviorally identifiable by the *one-beat pause* before a corrective remark, and by the practiced non-reaction to costumed weirdness.
- **Sibling-roast register** (the Khan kitchen, Nakia's commentary): sharp, fast, affection-coded. Operates as inoculation against external mockery — *we make fun of ourselves first and harder, so your contempt finds no purchase*.
- **Civic self-deprecation** ("it's Jersey, of course the train's late," "no one comes to Jersey on purpose"): a city-scaled in-joke that doubles as identity glue. Outsiders attempting this register without standing are immediately legible as outsiders.
- **Graffiti and signage humor** (Alphona-era backgrounds — misspelled storefronts, absurd flyers, the running visual gag of mundane chaos behind heroic foreground action): an *environmental* humor encoded into the built environment itself.

**Trigger:** any moment of potential awe, fear, or grandiosity. The neighborhood reflexively punctures all three.
**Cost:** occasional under-recognition of genuine danger; emotional vocabulary skews ironic, which can make sincere grief difficult to access until it overwhelms the joke (see the 2023 bereavement, where the humor went briefly silent).
**Failure mode:** when humor calcifies into cynicism — visible in the Hydra-collaborator faction's shrug at occupation ("what's the difference, it's still Jersey").

### 2. Altruism — institutionalized, not improvised

The mosque-as-shelter behavior during the *Last Days* event is the textbook example, but altruism in this subject is **structural rather than spontaneous**. Bruno's bodega running an informal tab for elderly customers; the Khan family's reflex to feed any teenager who enters the kitchen; Sheikh Abdullah's role as a mental-health first responder for a community without psychiatric infrastructure; Coles teachers staying late without overtime — these are *standing arrangements*, not crisis improvisations. The neighborhood has *pre-built* its altruistic capacity, which is why it mobilizes in minutes rather than days when stressed.

**Trigger:** any unmet need within the in-group radius (which is generously drawn — the in-group includes anyone present in the neighborhood, not only longtime residents).
**Cost:** chronic under-resourcing of caregivers; altruism is volunteered labor extracted from people already economically squeezed.
**Failure mode:** altruism-as-identity can prevent residents from asking for help themselves (Bruno's isolation in Wakanda; Aamir's unprocessed grief).

### 3. Sublimation — *the conversion of harm into public art*

The most aesthetically visible defense. Murals on Greenville walls (especially the post-2023 Kamala iconography), graffiti tags that double as mourning notices, hand-painted bodega signage, the wedding-decoration craft tradition visible in the Aamir/Tyesha sequences, the Coles theater and arts programming that absorbs adolescent volatility. The neighborhood **converts grief, rage, and disinvestment into surface ornament**. This is the same psychic operation that produced Harlem Renaissance muralism, Belfast peace walls, and East L.A.'s public iconography — a recognized civic-scale sublimative tradition.

**Trigger:** loss, anniversary, structural insult.
**Cost:** the harm gets memorialized but not necessarily redressed; beauty can substitute for justice.
**Failure mode:** when sublimation becomes the *only* response — when a mural is treated as adequate closure for a death that warranted a lawsuit.

### 4. Suppression (mature, conscious) — *not* repression

A specifically chosen postponement of affect. Visible in the Khan family's collective decision to keep the wedding on schedule despite Stormranger; in the neighborhood's decision to reopen the Circle Q the morning after each catastrophe; in the explicit "we'll deal with this later, right now we eat" rhythm of the kitchen scenes. This is conscious deferral, not denial — the feeling is acknowledged and *scheduled*, not banished.

**Trigger:** time-bounded events (weddings, prayers, school days, business hours) that anchor the community.
**Cost:** the "later" is often elastic; deferred affect accumulates.
**Failure mode:** indefinite deferral becomes functional repression (see §III).

### 5. Anticipation

Less obvious but present: the mosque's emergency-protocol behavior during *Last Days* implies prior rehearsal; the speed of the Inventor-era search networks implies pre-existing channels; the polish of the mutual-aid response to gentrification announcements implies that the neighborhood has *war-gamed displacement in advance*. The record never shows the rehearsal, only the readiness — which is itself diagnostic. This is a community that **expects bad things and pre-stages its response**.
